  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_34d9b624-00d5-4ec2-97ce-e7282d685d08'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div id="review_1449181264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1449181264" />
    <a title="Pinky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky"><img alt="Pinky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489855494p2/27523984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1449181264?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pinky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pinky" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky">Pinky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27523984-pinky?shelf=books-i-want-to-own">books-i-want-to-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1449181264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7960343338118920991"> I just...I can't even...It's so hard to find the perfect words to describe how I felt about this book.<br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402164056ra/9902159.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> I read both <i>Wonderstruck</i> and <i>The Invention of Hugo Cabret </i> and I loved both of them so much. Ever since those books, I couldn't stop thinking about how powerful they were. Brian Selznick is one of the most unique authors that I have read from. He uses pictures and words in a beautiful way and the stories connect and everything slides into place. <br/><br/> All of his books have a powerful meaning to th</span>
  <span id="freeText7960343338118920991" style="display:none"> I just...I can't even...It's so hard to find the perfect words to describe how I felt about this book.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1402164056ra/9902159.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> I read both <i>Wonderstruck</i> and <i>The Invention of Hugo Cabret </i> and I loved both of them so much. Ever since those books, I couldn't stop thinking about how powerful they were. Brian Selznick is one of the most unique authors that I have read from. He uses pictures and words in a beautiful way and the stories connect and everything slides into place. <br><br> All of his books have a powerful meaning to them and sometimes, it hurts so much to read this book because of the feels! But it is all worth it because it's hard to find a book like his. I experienced something so magical and beautiful, and when I finished the book, I was in tears. It was too good to be true and I was so shocked that I had finished the book.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419096ra/830491.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> This book is told both in both pictures and words, where the two stories collide and connect in some sort of way. The pictures are the story of the Marvels family, a family filled with actors and actresses and how their family became that famous. It shows the background of the Marvel family and how everyone is important. The words story is about a boy named Joseph who decides to run away with his friend Blink to his Uncle's house. But when Joseph was going to run away, Blink disappeared and Joseph has to run away all by himself.<br><br> While I was reading this book, I kept making crazy theories and I was thinking the same things Joseph was thinking. It messed with my brain so much and I loved that, it was so interesting to follow the different stories. All the stories made sense and everything seemed to fit in place in the end.<br><br> The characters were unique and I loved all of them, Florent, Albert, Joseph, Frankie, I could go on forever. They all were lovable in some sort of way and it felt like I had a connection with all of them. It was either because I felt they were easy to relate to or because they were so unique. So many characters were funny and made up for the depressing moments of the book. <br><br> Out of all of the books I read by Brian Selznick, I feel like this one was the most saddest one but awesome one at the same time. I can't pick a favorite out of all of his books because they are all beautiful and unique in their own way. I loved how this was kinda based off of a true story and how there was a huge note from Brian Selznick in the end.<br><br> Me and my friend were reading the first 40 pages together and we both loved it. The book is beautiful inside and out, I love how the edges of the pages are gold, it adds a look to the book. If I even wanted to be noticed by anyone, I could just carry this book around. (This book is so heavy, I felt like it was heavier than 3 of my textbooks combined, BUT THAT'S A GOOD THING!)<br><br> I highly, highly highly recommend that you read books by Brian Selznick, he is so unique and it is hard to find authors like him. I loved this book and hope to own it soon on my bookshelf, I don't want to return it. :( After reading this book, my hands were itching to reread it and I wanted to grab all of Brian Selznick's other books to read but I don't own them yet. I can't wait until the next book that Mr.Selznick will write, I am so excited! Anyway, I really hope you read this book, you will not regret it and this book will stay in your heart forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7960343338118920991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1530424382" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530424382" />
    <a title="jv poore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore"><img alt="jv poore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570108420p2/5157918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1530424382?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jv poore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jv poore" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore">jv poore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=buried-under-books">buried-under-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=own-it-arc">own-it-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1530424382" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12240220971794260412">I believe that, right before blowing out every single candle on the cake, a young reader somewhere made a spectacular wish for a book filled with gorgeous illustrations and a fabulous, fanciful story rich with quirky characters, adventure and mystery. Mr. Selznick fulfilled this wish in grand fashion.<br/><br/>To open The Marvels is to be immediately immersed in a harrowing adventure at sea. In the blink of an eye….or to be precise, the turn of several pages, invested in the story of a shipwreck with spun</span>
  <span id="freeText12240220971794260412" style="display:none">I believe that, right before blowing out every single candle on the cake, a young reader somewhere made a spectacular wish for a book filled with gorgeous illustrations and a fabulous, fanciful story rich with quirky characters, adventure and mystery. Mr. Selznick fulfilled this wish in grand fashion.<br /><br />To open The Marvels is to be immediately immersed in a harrowing adventure at sea. In the blink of an eye….or to be precise, the turn of several pages, invested in the story of a shipwreck with spunky survivors. Illustrations that seem to float above the pages “tell” a compelling, heart-tugging tale. Delightful drawings seem to reach out and wrap around the reader, securing you in the story well before Mr. Selznick weaves his word magic.<br /><br />When Mr. Selznick does put his pen to paper to write rather than draw, the result is no less stunning. His young, out-of-place-and-underfoot main character, Joseph, embodies awkward instances we’ve all endured. In his earnest desire to genuinely bond, to actually belong…he easily elicits empathy. <br /><br />When the sweet, stubborn boy tracks down his eclectic, enigmatic uncle in London, Joseph is sure he’s off to a terrible start. Genuine curiosity, compassionate neighbors and most importantly, time, make the reunion more palatable and the untold story of Joseph’s past is slowly revealed.<br /><br />In a sly, subtle shift, Mr. Selznick spins two separate, yet supporting stories in one brilliant book. Both with breathtaking backdrops: The Marvel family in the theatre and Joseph’s in his uncle’s frozen-in-time home. In the end, it seemed that I was moved by two different families. I was close, but not correct.<br /><br />My very favorite parts of the book occurred to me days after I’d finished the story. Mr. Selznick managed to encompass serious social issues such as loss, suddenly and inexplicably; alongside of loss that is excruciating slow, as two men deeply in love are both infected with AIDS. Intrigued and impressed, I finished the book by reading the Afterword, where Mr. Selznick sprung one more surprise. A large part of this fantasy is based loosely on the lives of two very real people. <br /><br />This review was written for Buried Under Books by jv poore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12240220971794260412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer2228810074442270579">2.5 stars<br/><br/>Obviously Selznick does amazing things. His art is fantastic and I love that he basically writes highly sophisticated picture books. I’d love to see more books follow his example actually. That said, I didn’t find the story contained in The Marvels particularly compelling.<br/><br/>There’s actually not really a plot here at all. I mean, there’s the pseudo-mystery of Joseph’s uncle’s house, but really not much happens in this book at all. There’s something aged about this book, and I don’t mean th</span>
  <span id="freeText2228810074442270579" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />Obviously Selznick does amazing things. His art is fantastic and I love that he basically writes highly sophisticated picture books. I’d love to see more books follow his example actually. That said, I didn’t find the story contained in The Marvels particularly compelling.<br /><br />There’s actually not really a plot here at all. I mean, there’s the pseudo-mystery of Joseph’s uncle’s house, but really not much happens in this book at all. There’s something aged about this book, and I don’t mean the historical setting. It seems more almost to be about Albert than about his nephew.<br /><br />It didn’t help that the start, the illustrated tale of the Marvels was so much more interesting than the text part. It might have been a more even tale for me had Joseph learned bits of the story as he searched the house, so the illustrations were mixed in.<br /><br />Worth a read because it’s short and Selznick is worth checking out, but not one I’ll be revisiting.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer12418465510634244623">The Marvels, Brian Selznick<br/><br/>Brian Selznick once again plays with the form, he invented and takes readers on an awe-inspiring voyage! Two seemingly unrelated stories-one in words, the other in pictures-come together with spellbinding synergy! The illustrated story begins in 1766 with Billy Marvel, the lone survivor of a shipwreck, and charts the adventures of his family of actors over five generations. <br/><br/>The prose story opens in 1990 and follows Joseph, who has run away from school to an estranged u</span>
  <span id="freeText12418465510634244623" style="display:none">The Marvels, Brian Selznick<br /><br />Brian Selznick once again plays with the form, he invented and takes readers on an awe-inspiring voyage! Two seemingly unrelated stories-one in words, the other in pictures-come together with spellbinding synergy! The illustrated story begins in 1766 with Billy Marvel, the lone survivor of a shipwreck, and charts the adventures of his family of actors over five generations. <br /><br />The prose story opens in 1990 and follows Joseph, who has run away from school to an estranged uncle’s puzzling house in London, where he, along with the reader, must piece together many mysteries. How the picture and word stories intersect will leave readers marveling over Selznick’s storytelling prowess. Filled with mystery, vibrant characters, surprise twists, and heartrending beauty, and featuring Selznick's most arresting art to date, The Marvels is a moving tribute to the power of story.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه اکتبر سال 2019 میلدی<br /><br />عنوان: مارولز؛ نویسنده: برايان سلزنيک؛<br /><br />از«برايان سلزنيک» پیشتر کتابهای «اختراع هوگو کابره؛ در پانصد و هشتاد و یک صفحه، برگردان: رضی هيرمندی»؛ و «شگفت‌زده، در ششصد و نود و پنج صفحه، برگردان: رضی هیرمندی»؛ نوشیده ایم. ساختار کتابهای ایشان ترکیبی ناهمزمان از تصویر و نوشتار هستند؛ خوانشگر کتاب را همچون یک فیلم میبیند و میخواند. در این کتاب نیز تصاویر جای خالی بخشهایی از قصه را پر میکنند که در متن نیامده است. ا. شربیانی</span>

<div id="review_1424895186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424895186" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424895186?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=new-favorites">new-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1424895186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17361015035568788853">Breathtaking.<br/><br/>I've seen some people who don't love this book, and their reasons seem to mostly be because it's different from his others. Instead of the pictures being intermingled with the text, there is one complete story told in pictures for the first 2/3rds of the pages, then a story entirely in text for the rest of the book. But there's a reason why, and the reason is a very startling twist, and I loved it. <br/><br/>His prose is very straightforward, simple really, and almost as quick to read as the </span>
  <span id="freeText17361015035568788853" style="display:none">Breathtaking.<br /><br />I've seen some people who don't love this book, and their reasons seem to mostly be because it's different from his others. Instead of the pictures being intermingled with the text, there is one complete story told in pictures for the first 2/3rds of the pages, then a story entirely in text for the rest of the book. But there's a reason why, and the reason is a very startling twist, and I loved it. <br /><br />His prose is very straightforward, simple really, and almost as quick to read as the pictures, yet when you're done you're left with this amazing mental image of all these people and their lives. It's absolutely gorgeous. I also think I was ready to fall in love with the book, too, because I got it at an event where he first talked and showed pictures for over an hour. He covered his process in creating his books (the pictures, in real life, are TINY and it would be like designing a dollar bill over and over again!), and he also talked about the inspiration for this book, and the real life places that he explored and used for models. I don't want to spoil anything, but it's wonderful, and there's an afterword in the book discussing some of that. I also think it interesting that the format of the book is a form that he's exploring. In HUGO he told one story with pictures and words. In WONDERSTRUCK he wanted to tell two linked stories, one with pictures and one with words, going back and forth, but with this book he purposely decided to tell one entire story with pictures, and one entire story with words, but not mix them together. <br /><br />This worked for me, I think also because the book itself is so beautiful. The colors, the cover, the gilded edges, the beautiful paper quality, all just made my little bookworm heart swoon. I'd pick this as a hot contender for whatever awards they can give it, and I hope it wins. It's my favorite of the three, which he considers an unofficial trilogy (THE INVENTION OF HUGO CABRET, WONDERSTRUCK, THE MARVELS).<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17361015035568788853" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1194386141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1194386141" />
    <a title="Monica Edinger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/221952-monica-edinger"><img alt="Monica Edinger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427102957p2/221952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1194386141?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica Edinger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica Edinger" href="/user/show/221952-monica-edinger">Monica Edinger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194386141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18199772454131640697"><a href='https://medinger.wordpress.com/2015/05/30/coming-soon-brian-selznicks-the-marvels/' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog review. </a><br/><br/>Brian Selznick is one of the great artists of our time. In what is now a trilogy (<em>The Invention of Hugo Cabret, Wonderstruck, </em>and now<a href='http://www.amazon.com/The-Marvels-Brian-Selznick/dp/0545448689' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <em> The Marvels</em>
</a>) he has created a unique storytelling style, one that blends illustration and text in an engrossingly original way. It is an aesthetic and emotive experience not like that of a graphic novel, but one closer to a cinematic viewing experience or a theatrical one; the three books are rich with scenes of powerful beauty created with pap</span>
  <span id="freeText18199772454131640697" style="display:none"><a href="https://medinger.wordpress.com/2015/05/30/coming-soon-brian-selznicks-the-marvels/" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog review. </a><br /><br />Brian Selznick is one of the great artists of our time. In what is now a trilogy (<em>The Invention of Hugo Cabret, Wonderstruck, </em>and now<a href="http://www.amazon.com/The-Marvels-Brian-Selznick/dp/0545448689" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em> The Marvels</em>
</a>) he has created a unique storytelling style, one that blends illustration and text in an engrossingly original way. It is an aesthetic and emotive experience not like that of a graphic novel, but one closer to a cinematic viewing experience or a theatrical one; the three books are rich with scenes of powerful beauty created with paper, page turns, close-ups, and more. Upon completing <em>The Marvels</em>, I sat still, feeling as I did after a remarkable theatrical experience, say a dramatic opera, a visually stunning film, or a striking play, in awe of what I'd just experienced. Hours later it lingers with me, a gorgeous work of art.<br /><br /><em>The Marvels</em> begins in the 18th century with images, hundreds of pages of them relating a mysterious story of a theatrical family over several generations. Ships and theaters, riggings and scenery, weather and atmosphere, adventure and drama, light and dark, youth and age, convention and strangeness  --- it is all there. Midway the images end and it is 1990 with a story now told exclusively in words. We meet Joseph who has run away from boarding school and is now in London desperately seeking out the one address he knows: 18 Folgate Street where his uncle lives, someone he knows nothing about and has never met. A fortunate encounter with a child his own age finally brings him to his relative who is not at all happy that he has come. There are mysteries galore --- that of Joseph's uncle's remarkable house, of Joseph's friend from school who has disappeared, of his and his uncle's family, and of another one called the Marvels. By the end, the first two parts of the book are made whole in a brief, but powerful and brave conclusion, told again in drawings, set in the present day.<br /><br />The book was inspired by a remarkable man, <a href="http://www.theguardian.com/news/2000/jan/10/guardianobituaries" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Dennis Severs</a>, <a href="http://www.dennissevershouse.co.uk/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">his house</a> in London at 18 Folgate Street, and his friend David Milne. My own familiarity with their story, <a href="https://medinger.wordpress.com/2012/08/23/london-day-two-dennis-sever-and-matilda/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">visit to the house a few years </a>ago, and experiences during the period of the second part of the novel made my reading of <em>The Marvels </em>both aesthetically powerful and personally significant. As Joseph's story and that of his uncle's and his house began to unfold I started to recognize aspects of it and had a premonition as to where the story was going, causing me to remember others, artists I knew and cared for so much and whose lives were all too brief. And so I know that my reading was quite likely different from that of someone without my background, especially child readers.<br /><br />Thank you, Brian, for <em>The Marvels</em>, for creating this work of art that remembers, looks behind and ahead, that celebrates the power of love, of art, of books, and the future with extraordinary art, grace, and elegance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18199772454131640697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6711210571482828970">Another wonderful, unique book with wonderful storylines and beautiful illustrations. After around half the book being a story of illustrations and no text, we meet Joseph, a run away, equally unhappy at school as at home, he has uninterested parents who are not present in his life and he doesn't fit in at school. Running away he reaches his uncle Andrew, whose artistic, museum like house gives Joseph a safe haven, a place to fit in and a mystery to solve. A book about discovering who you are an</span>
  <span id="freeText6711210571482828970" style="display:none">Another wonderful, unique book with wonderful storylines and beautiful illustrations. After around half the book being a story of illustrations and no text, we meet Joseph, a run away, equally unhappy at school as at home, he has uninterested parents who are not present in his life and he doesn't fit in at school. Running away he reaches his uncle Andrew, whose artistic, museum like house gives Joseph a safe haven, a place to fit in and a mystery to solve. A book about discovering who you are and coping with the loss of loved ones. I appreciated the acknowledgement that a happy family doesn't always involve the parents you were born to and I enjoyed the end pages of factual information about the story.</span>

<div id="review_1583446216" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1583446216" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1583446216?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1583446216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17549449921595529536">This book was magnificent and is solidly tied with Wonderstruck (also by Selznick) for my favourite of his three books. This one is formatted slightly differently from the previous two becuase it's half told in pictures and half told in text, but unlike his previous works the pictures do not dissect the text, rather there is one section of solid imagery and one section of solid text. <br/><br/>This is the story of the Marvels, a family of actors with great notoriety and a wonderful past on the stage. This</span>
  <span id="freeText17549449921595529536" style="display:none">This book was magnificent and is solidly tied with Wonderstruck (also by Selznick) for my favourite of his three books. This one is formatted slightly differently from the previous two becuase it's half told in pictures and half told in text, but unlike his previous works the pictures do not dissect the text, rather there is one section of solid imagery and one section of solid text. <br /><br />This is the story of the Marvels, a family of actors with great notoriety and a wonderful past on the stage. This story is then woven together with Joseph, a young boy who just wants to get away from his boarding school and so he goes to visit his uncle (who he's never before met) in London. As these two stories compare the image-based one took me far less time to get into, but the text story really drew everything together and I do have to admit I did shed some tears because it really was a beautiful and sad tale.<br />Some of the elements Selznick weaves into this story felt more modern with same sex couples and other interesting family dynamics playing a role. I really liked seeing this as I felt it worked incredibly well and felt totally natural within the story.<br /><br />Finally, as always with Selznick, I have to say the artwork is stunning and the pencil images always draw you in and make you anxious to see what will happen next because they are like little stop-frames of what's actually going on. <br /><br />For me, this was excellent, and although the format was a little more of an adjustment for me, it paid off hugely as it hit me hard and was a wonderful tale. 5*s really recommended... My only problem now is that I have run out of Selznick books and I know I will be buying whatever he brings out in the future!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17549449921595529536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1418506545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418506545" />
    <a title="Suad Shamma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma"><img alt="Suad Shamma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507364224p2/11245979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1418506545?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suad Shamma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suad Shamma" href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma">Suad Shamma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418506545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13497854169246737236">I was very disappointed by this book. Perhaps I should have read more into it before blindly buying it, but I bought it spontaneously because of the beautiful cover and the mysteriously magical synopsis. Also Brian Selznick is known for his fantastical stories, such as Hugo, and I expected no less from this one. <br/><br/>I was all set to read about this family's eccentric life of theatre and peculiar characters and the mysteries behind the house and so on. Instead, all I got was this strangely boring sto</span>
  <span id="freeText13497854169246737236" style="display:none">I was very disappointed by this book. Perhaps I should have read more into it before blindly buying it, but I bought it spontaneously because of the beautiful cover and the mysteriously magical synopsis. Also Brian Selznick is known for his fantastical stories, such as Hugo, and I expected no less from this one. <br /><br />I was all set to read about this family's eccentric life of theatre and peculiar characters and the mysteries behind the house and so on. Instead, all I got was this strangely boring story of a boy who ran away from school to his uncle's place in London, hoping to find his best friend who had run away before him. He finds all these strange occurrences at his uncle's house and with the help of the neighbor's daughter tries to find out more about his family's history. And when he thinks he has it all figured out, his uncle confesses that it is all a lie and that their history is actually quite ordinary and not very interesting. <br /><br />I was let down, and I felt like I had wasted so much of my time on this book. Not to mention that the entire first half of this really big book is filled with haphazard drawings that really weren't to my taste. Obviously, that is a personal preference. It seems a lot of the other readers found the artwork to be magnificent, but it wasn't for me. It's not my style, and it was difficult to keep up with what was going on just by the illustrations. I found myself quickly skipping through the drawings to get to the actual story and try to understand what was happening and what I had missed. The thing is, that in itself seemed like a waste of time and paper as well, because Selznick repeats everything he had conveyed in his drawings in the written part of the book, having us go through it twice. <br /><br />Only to find out it was all made up of course.<br /><br />A story within a story so to speak. And not the most exciting one. <br /><br />In addition to that, I did not like the characters, and so I was not invested in what happened to them. In fact, my least favorite character was the girl - dressed as a boy - who was extremely irritating to me. I think the fact that I can't actually remember any of the characters' names speaks volumes of how I feel about the book. So I'll just leave it at that. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13497854169246737236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1327391050" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1327391050" />
    <a title="Bonnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie"><img alt="Bonnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604440764p2/5136858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1327391050?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5136858-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5136858-bonnie?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327391050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13650524158169072525">Continuing his unique theme of storytelling, Selznick takes his readers on a dual adventure told in pictures and then words. The first adventure is experienced solely in pictures and begins in 1776 on a ship named the Kraken. After a massive storm, there is only a single survivor: Billy Marvel. The pictures tell of his story, how he came to be connected to the Royal Theatre in London, and how subsequent generations became well-known actors with their own story to tell. The visually impressive il</span>
  <span id="freeText13650524158169072525" style="display:none">Continuing his unique theme of storytelling, Selznick takes his readers on a dual adventure told in pictures and then words. The first adventure is experienced solely in pictures and begins in 1776 on a ship named the Kraken. After a massive storm, there is only a single survivor: Billy Marvel. The pictures tell of his story, how he came to be connected to the Royal Theatre in London, and how subsequent generations became well-known actors with their own story to tell. The visually impressive illustrated story continues for over 400 pages and ends with an air of mystery.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441988704i/16178020._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Flashing forward to the 1990s, we’re introduced to Joseph Jervis who has just ran away from boarding school to go in search of his Uncle Albert. Joseph’s parents are the absent sort and he’s hoping to find a family, a place to call home. Finding his Uncle ends up being a letdown seeing as he wants to immediately send Joseph back to where he belongs and doesn’t show any interest in getting to know each other. Joseph takes comfort in his Uncle’s old house that’s filled with history and a certain story that Joseph desperately wants to uncover. While the story of Joseph is an intriguing one, what’s more intriguing is how his story and that of Billy Marvel’s, two seemingly isolated stories, could possibly be connected. The connection slowly begins to piece together, flowering into a beautifully simplistic story about love and family.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441988705i/16178021._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really adored this story; it even managed to elicit some teary-eyed feels. I loved the combination of pictures/words and was most impressed that Selznick managed to make his words-only storytelling just as mentally visual as his illustrations-only story. This charmingly simplistic story won me over completely and I definitely intend on picking up all of Selznick’s other works.<br><br>Many thanks to Wendy for gifting me this lovely story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13650524158169072525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This book was incredible. I loved everything about it - hands down my favorite from Selznick yet. I had no idea where this was going, none at all.   <span id="freeText10196415673655478645" style="display:none">Don't let the length of time I spent on this book fool you, we were right in the middle of end-of-the-year school madness so I was forced to put it (and everything else) down for a while. This book was incredible. I loved everything about it - hands down my favorite from Selznick yet. I had no idea where this was going, none at all. I thought I had it figured out but I was so very far from close. When I had to put it down halfway through due to work, I thought I knew where it was going so imagine my surprise when I picked it up again and went hurdling in an entirely new direction! I stayed up long into the night to finish after that. I want to badly to say more, but I couldn't spoil it for you like that. It is beyond marvelous and I highly recommend it.</span>

<div id="review_2057019532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2057019532" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2057019532?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=histiorical">histiorical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-middle-grade">bage-middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-mystery">genre-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-shakespeare">z-shakespeare</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=z-brian-selznick">z-brian-selznick</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=want-to-own">want-to-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-drama-tragedy">genre-drama-tragedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2057019532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15792822495968471940">Brian Selznick has made a 3rd masterpiece in a row. This book is about good stories, Shakespeare, Ships, and hard life experiences. I like how straight forward the gay uncle is presented. This book is about layers and creating your own life. The art is beautiful in the book and the outside is gorgeous also. I will miss having this story to read. It was incredible. It is so well told - really. If you are going to read any middle grade, try Brian Selznick after Harry Potter. Also, if you like grap</span>
  <span id="freeText15792822495968471940" style="display:none">Brian Selznick has made a 3rd masterpiece in a row. This book is about good stories, Shakespeare, Ships, and hard life experiences. I like how straight forward the gay uncle is presented. This book is about layers and creating your own life. The art is beautiful in the book and the outside is gorgeous also. I will miss having this story to read. It was incredible. It is so well told - really. If you are going to read any middle grade, try Brian Selznick after Harry Potter. Also, if you like graphic novels, this is a great gateway into part novel part graphic novel of sorts. I was moved by this book. It looks long and it's only about 250 pages of words really. It should be on anyone's reading list.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1323453465" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1323453465" />
    <a title="Donna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6217162-donna"><img alt="Donna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430955688p2/6217162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1323453465?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/6217162-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6217162-donna?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1323453465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10655521171803078567">I wasn't sure about reading this book since I am one of the few people who wasn't bowled over by another of the author's books, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret' title='The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a>. I enjoyed the illustrations in that book, but I thought the characters and the story lacked depth. Not so in the case of this book which had not one but two stories to tell, each of them amazing in their own right, and doubly so as they intertwined. Unfortunately, I can't tell you much about them without spoiling things. But what I will say</span>
  <span id="freeText10655521171803078567" style="display:none">I wasn't sure about reading this book since I am one of the few people who wasn't bowled over by another of the author's books, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret" title="The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a>. I enjoyed the illustrations in that book, but I thought the characters and the story lacked depth. Not so in the case of this book which had not one but two stories to tell, each of them amazing in their own right, and doubly so as they intertwined. Unfortunately, I can't tell you much about them without spoiling things. But what I will say is this: this book is unique in its design with the first 387 pages containing a story told strictly through illustrations. These aren't colorful illustrations. Rather, they were created by the author using pencil and charcoal to form highly expressive scenes brimming with emotions conveyed through shadow and light. <br /><br />This first story begins in 1766, when young Billy Marvel becomes the only survivor of a shipwreck, and without family and money, and against all odds, goes on to found five generations of actors at a famous London theater. This generational story was fascinating, made even more so by the fact that pictures alone conveyed it, in all its intricacies. And when it finally came to an end, I quickly flipped to the page where the next story began, one told only in words. <br /><br />This second story begins in 1990, ninety years after the end of the previous story. This story focuses on another young boy named Joseph Jervis who, neglected by his rich parents and misunderstood, runs away from his boarding school to find an uncle in London he's never met and knows little about. What he finds along with his uncle is his uncle's strange and mysterious house that proves a puzzle to Joseph as much as his uncle and his own family history. Joseph sets off with the help of a friend to solve a mystery that leads to others he must solve if he is ever to learn the truth about his family and himself. <br /><br />By the end of this book, these two seemingly separate stories collided in a most unusual and creative way to form yet a third story that was rich and deep, and filled with characters that were three dimensional, imperfect and highly sympathetic to the reader as their stories unfolded, layer upon layer. And as if this weren't enough, yet another story is revealed in the afterword when the author and illustrator, Mr. Selznick, tells of his inspiration for this book. Don't miss reading this section which is incredible. <br /><br />This book is both satisfying and suitable for adults and children ten years of age and older. As a note, there are some mature elements in the second story concerning Joseph's uncle which are dealt with sensitively and are a credit to the author who bravely included them in a children's book. <br /><br />This is a wonderful and imaginative book for people who enjoy mysteries. It's also beautiful in its design with a striking cover and gold edged pages that form a reflective surface along three sides of the book. Don't be put off by its hefty size of 665 pages since more than half are filled with illustrations, the rest with an intriguing and emotionally satisfying story I'm glad I read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10655521171803078567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1171504507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171504507" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1171504507?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1171504507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6234968312127861482"><b>
  <i>“That’s what life is, Joseph realized, miracles and sadness, side by side.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>I fell in love with Brian Selznick's artwork in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret' title='The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a>, which I think is the reason I keep coming back to read his new books. I love the way his sketchbook-style, beautiful charcoal drawings resemble movie scenes, with the pages zooming in on characters' expressions.<br/><br/><a href='http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpswhyf6br3.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445715169i/16694948._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo image_zpswhyf6br3.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>There are pages and pages of these wonderful drawings.<br/><br/><a href='http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpsgn6hz4a1.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445715768i/16695011._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo image_zpsgn6hz4a1.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The thing is, although I've always found Selznick's artwork stunning, </span>
  <span id="freeText6234968312127861482" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“That’s what life is, Joseph realized, miracles and sadness, side by side.”</i>
</b><br><br>I fell in love with Brian Selznick's artwork in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret" title="The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a>, which I think is the reason I keep coming back to read his new books. I love the way his sketchbook-style, beautiful charcoal drawings resemble movie scenes, with the pages zooming in on characters' expressions.<br><br><a href="http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpswhyf6br3.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445715169i/16694948._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpswhyf6br3.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There are pages and pages of these wonderful drawings.<br><br><a href="http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpsgn6hz4a1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445715768i/16695011._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpsgn6hz4a1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The thing is, although I've always found Selznick's artwork stunning, his stories seem much weaker in comparison. Plot wise, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9673436.The_Invention_of_Hugo_Cabret" title="The Invention of Hugo Cabret by Brian Selznick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Invention of Hugo Cabret</a> was my favorite because I enjoyed the mysterious story of a boy living in a clock tower in a train station, stealing food to survive.<br><br><a href="http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpsqlnhgjvf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445715768i/16695012._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpsqlnhgjvf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Selznick's later works, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10128428.Wonderstruck" title="Wonderstruck by Brian Selznick" rel="nofollow noopener">Wonderstruck</a> and now <i>The Marvels</i>, both have very simplistic story lines that I never found too intriguing. They usually have some nice themes about family or friendship, but the characters just aren't complex enough, the plots not quite as exciting as I'd like them to be.<br><br>In <i>The Marvels</i>, the story follows a line of theater actors (in pictures) and years later, Joseph, who runs away to his uncle's strange house in London (in words).<br><br><a href="http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpsqogfapfc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445714813i/16694925._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpsqogfapfc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The way <i>The Marvels</i> ended was a bit strange for me, or else I probably would have rated it four stars because I really loved the four hundred pages of gorgeous artwork. I'm sure I'll fall prey to whatever Selznick publishes next just to get another taste of his mesmerizing drawings.<br><br><a href="http://s292.photobucket.com/user/drewjreader/media/Mobile%20Uploads/image_zpsbel1ijse.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <a title="Roya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12222982-roya"><img alt="Roya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566487407p2/12222982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roya" href="/user/show/12222982-roya">Roya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12222982-roya?shelf=quite-good">quite-good</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2708688595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16916068046557494846">I think this is one of those books I'll enjoy more with the passing of time. It gives you something to think about without being predictable. Out of all the books by Selznick I've read, this is probably the most dialogue focused. I don't think it's his strongest work, but it's worth reading all the same. Discovering how much research really went into making this book was also fascinating. I'd love to pay a visit to the house one day.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1783962186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1783962186" />
    <a title="Shoa Khan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23794303-shoa-khan"><img alt="Shoa Khan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520966559p2/23794303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1783962186?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shoa Khan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shoa Khan" href="/user/show/23794303-shoa-khan">Shoa Khan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=historific">historific</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=choice-awards-2015">choice-awards-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=br-with-prince">br-with-prince</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=tamu-library">tamu-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=2015-releases">2015-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=graphix-card">graphix-card</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23794303-shoa-khan?shelf=ir-armchair-travels-2017">ir-armchair-travels-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1783962186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3838174879360809776">I sometimes feel that Brian Selznick doesn't belong to this era. How he manages to find all these interesting true stories and characters is beyond me. <br/>Told in his signature style, the story of the Marvels is seeped in old-world charm. This book features two intertwined stories from two different centuries - one in prose and the other entirely in pictures. As always, the illustrations are intricately beautiful. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487924695i/22064115._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And the story is about as mysterious as it gets. Although I felt the mystery bit was </span>
  <span id="freeText3838174879360809776" style="display:none">I sometimes feel that Brian Selznick doesn't belong to this era. How he manages to find all these interesting true stories and characters is beyond me. <br>Told in his signature style, the story of the Marvels is seeped in old-world charm. This book features two intertwined stories from two different centuries - one in prose and the other entirely in pictures. As always, the illustrations are intricately beautiful. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487924695i/22064115._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the story is about as mysterious as it gets. Although I felt the mystery bit was a bit drawn out, but then that could be because of the amount of time it took me to read the book! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487924695i/22064116._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This time around, the awe-inspiring element wasn't that strong either.<br>But the extra star is for the fact that the fascinating, out-of-this-world place mentioned in the book actually exists! It makes me want to visit it some day!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100019173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7829518259273524548">Well this was a strange one. The best I can say is the artwork was lovely. The first 400 pages of pencil sketches outline an interesting story of the Marvel family and spans a period of time from the 1760s until 1900. I liked where this story was going, it seemed to promise adventure, theatrical shenanigans and a kind of earnest delight in all things English. Selznick sketches facial features extremely well, particular adorable babies.<br/><br/>The remainder of the book unfortunately reverts to what I fou</span>
  <span id="freeText7829518259273524548" style="display:none">Well this was a strange one. The best I can say is the artwork was lovely. The first 400 pages of pencil sketches outline an interesting story of the Marvel family and spans a period of time from the 1760s until 1900. I liked where this story was going, it seemed to promise adventure, theatrical shenanigans and a kind of earnest delight in all things English. Selznick sketches facial features extremely well, particular adorable babies.<br /><br />The remainder of the book unfortunately reverts to what I found to be dull and pedestrian prose. The setting is now 1990s Spitalfields, although weirdly it is impossible to reconcile this as everyone still behaves like characters in a Dickens novel. Possibly the most incongruous part being a horse drawn carriage taken to the theatre in 1990s London ? Does that still happen ? Where do you even park it ? Anyway .... I didn't gel with this part at all, it just seemed to go nowhere and take so long to do it. Disappointing after such a promising start. Also what ever happened to Blink ? <br /><br />The afterward in the book details the real people and places that were used as inspiration for this story, which does help make clear what Brian Selznick was aiming for with <i> The Marvels </i>. Its a shame the writing just didn't hold up to the task. <br /><br />( Also, contrary to some frankly puzzling one star reviews of this, I thought the very subtle LGBT themes in this were quite charmingly done and targeted appropriately to the intended age group. )</span>
  <a data-text-id="7829518259273524548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1421210930" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1421210930" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1421210930?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1421210930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5286261483532166584">Selznick has his own particular style: books that are part prose and mostly pages of his beautiful, wordless pencils. I can't think of any other author who does this on a regular basis, and very few ever try it at all. I think this just might be my favorite of his books. That's probably because the art and the words are quite separate in the book, which makes sense. They cover different time spans. The first section of art (about 400 pages long) is the history of a theatrical family, and it's ea</span>
  <span id="freeText5286261483532166584" style="display:none">Selznick has his own particular style: books that are part prose and mostly pages of his beautiful, wordless pencils. I can't think of any other author who does this on a regular basis, and very few ever try it at all. I think this just might be my favorite of his books. That's probably because the art and the words are quite separate in the book, which makes sense. They cover different time spans. The first section of art (about 400 pages long) is the history of a theatrical family, and it's easy to follow though only the first character, Billy, and the last, Leo, were really given any depth. Then there's about 150 pages of straight writing, set in the early 80s. It's about a boy, Joseph, who runs off to his uncle's mysterious house. I liked Joseph, but the mystery felt a little drawn out to me. It's the sort of mystery that's only mysterious because people are outright refusing to talk, which I tend to find frustrating. It was saved because of how much I liked Joseph, and because I actually was surprised by the outcome. And then it's wrapped up with another 50 or so pages of art, set in the present day. Which means that this is indeed a doorstopper of a book. And a book that can be read in just a few hours. There's nothing like a Brian Selznick book to inflate your page counts. At any rate, I got attached enough to Joseph in particular, as well as a few other characters, to really like this book overall.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5286261483532166584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1407888021" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1407888021" />
    <a title="Amerie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8636182-amerie"><img alt="Amerie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494714012p2/8636182.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1407888021?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amerie" href="/user/show/8636182-amerie">Amerie</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407888021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8556927861500980916">Mr. Selznick's drawing are powerful when it comes to capturing human facial expressions, especially the eyes. I enjoyed the seemingly irrelevant clues placed within drawings--numbers, directed gazes, etc. When I reached the prose section of the story, however, I felt my attention flag, but that was to be expected as a new story (seemingly) was beginning. I patiently waited for both stories to converge, and when they did (in an unexpected way), <b>I appreciated the author's attempt to encapsulate th</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8556927861500980916" style="display:none">Mr. Selznick's drawing are powerful when it comes to capturing human facial expressions, especially the eyes. I enjoyed the seemingly irrelevant clues placed within drawings--numbers, directed gazes, etc. When I reached the prose section of the story, however, I felt my attention flag, but that was to be expected as a new story (seemingly) was beginning. I patiently waited for both stories to converge, and when they did (in an unexpected way), <b>I appreciated the author's attempt to encapsulate the scope of life's harshest realities into a single prose-picture book.</b> It definitely took an unexpected turn. Themes and topics such as <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[love and loss and AIDs and fear and hate <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were subtly done and as someone who appreciates a multi-generational story, this magical tale and its poignant ending will stay with me for a long time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8556927861500980916" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

This book didn't disappoint my expectations and is amazing just as the first book I've read. <br/></span>

  <span id="freeText10158262518963327832" style="display:none">This is an advanced copy.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the beginning of the story--the pictures and the family history of the Marvels. This was definitely the gem of the book. However, I was disappointed, like the character named Joseph, when there wasn't a continuation to that portion of the book, and I felt cheated that in the book's universe that the Marvels weren't real. Onto the text of the story, I liked it for the most part, but I did not feel a connection or a pull to any of the characters. I felt that the end was really sappy and that it fell flat. The stories are charming and engrossing at the beginning, but the ending does not match the beginning with the same level of magic and wonder. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1407466798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11456606179285878736">About 2/3rds of this 600-page volume tells the story of the Marvel family in Brian Selznick's extraordinary illustrations. Most of the way through, he launches into the story of a young boy running away from his prep school to find his estranged uncle in London. This part of the book moves a bit, but not overly, slowly; it supplements and explains more about the illustrated portion. The London story is based in a beautifully restored mansion in a dodgy part of the city, and a real place. I found</span>
  <span id="freeText11456606179285878736" style="display:none">About 2/3rds of this 600-page volume tells the story of the Marvel family in Brian Selznick's extraordinary illustrations. Most of the way through, he launches into the story of a young boy running away from his prep school to find his estranged uncle in London. This part of the book moves a bit, but not overly, slowly; it supplements and explains more about the illustrated portion. The London story is based in a beautifully restored mansion in a dodgy part of the city, and a real place. I found the relationship between the runaway and his uncle to be quite uneven, explained in part by a French carriage driver.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11456606179285878736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OU7yPsKY9kD7hH0TmNk3ejCcAQA6ntHyFCGjmzMzZAYNSCFEEflKr6dMz0baqlZIv9b6yLBOmHgL315T9nXAKw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Y4IRlA8mqN3OFHaMX0h9snkdzDkOpJh2m4B0Iu+WuddXhMLu3EcUMpLcxNkdOxyA9lc38YR00fyEfonqKtAd+g==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/38120.Brian_Selznick">About Brian Selznick</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/38120.Brian_Selznick"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201028714p3/38120.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/38120.Brian_Selznick">Brian Selznick

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18158216722966522191">Hello there. My name is Brian Selznick and I’m the author and illustrator of The Invention of Hugo Cabret. I was born in 1966 in New Jersey. I have a sister who is a teacher, a brother who is a brain surgeon, and five nephews and one niece. I studied at The Rhode Island School of Design and after I graduated from college I worked at Eeyore’s Books for Children in New York City. I learned all about</span>
  <span id="freeText18158216722966522191" style="display:none">Hello there. My name is Brian Selznick and I’m the author and illustrator of The Invention of Hugo Cabret. I was born in 1966 in New Jersey. I have a sister who is a teacher, a brother who is a brain surgeon, and five nephews and one niece. I studied at The Rhode Island School of Design and after I graduated from college I worked at Eeyore’s Books for Children in New York City. I learned all about children’s books from my boss Steve Geck who is now an editor of children’s books at Greenwillow. While I was at Eeyore’s I also painted the windows for holidays and book events. <br /><br />My first book, The Houdini Box, which I both wrote and illustrated, was published in 1991 while I was still working at the bookstore. Since then, I have illustrated many books for children, including Frindle by Andrew Clements, The Doll People by Ann Martin and Laura Godwin, Amelia and Eleanor Go for a Ride by Pam Muñoz Ryan and The Dinosaurs of Waterhouse Hawkins by Barbara Kerley, which received a 2001 Caldecott Honor.<br /><br />I have also written a few other books myself, including The Boy of a Thousand Faces, but The Invention of Hugo Cabret is by far the longest and most involved book I’ve ever worked on. <br /><br />I live in Brooklyn, New York, and San Diego, California.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18158216722966522191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/43165888-the-marvels">Quotes from The Marvels</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Maybe the play wasn't about miracles. No, maybe it was about the passage of time, and the need for patience, and the ability to forgive. Maybe Shakespeare was saying that even in a world where miracles can happen, there's still going to be pain, and loss, and regret. Because sometimes people die and you can't bring them back. That's what life is Joseph realized, miracles and sadness, side by side.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7436235-maybe-the-play-wasn-t-about-miracles-no-maybe-it-was">17 likes</a>
            </nobr>
